## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P(t), which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. Common relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects, and time-varying environmental forcing via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant source/sink added to exponential growth)
- Power-law (generalized per-capita scaling): dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (density-dependent scaling when reproduction is non-linear in P)
- Logistic growth ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (carrying capacity via c1 < 0; quadratic density dependence)
- Logistic with linear harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 * P (extra proportional loss/gain term)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (constant removal/addition regardless of P)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines ~log(P), common in microbial/tumor growth)
- Rational saturating recruitment minus mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) + c2 * P (recruitment saturates at high P; c2 often < 0 for mortality)
- Exponential crowding inhibition: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (crowding reduces growth when c1 < 0; smooth alternative to logistic)
- Strong Allee effect (cubic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (c2 + c3 * P) (captures low-density suppression and high-density limitation with suitable signs)
- Seasonally forced per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting growth rate)
- Time-trending environment (nonstationary r): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P + c2 * P**2 (gradual change in growth conditions over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence shows up as nonlinear terms in P (e.g., P^2, P^(1+theta)) causing per-capita growth (dP_dt/P) to decline with P.
- A carrying capacity is typically implied when dP_dt changes sign at a positive equilibrium P*: include factors like (1 + c*P) or (1 + c*P^theta) with c < 0.
- Allee effects (poor growth at low density) require dP_dt to be negative for small positive P, often produced by higher-order polynomials in P with a positive root at the Allee threshold.
- Separating recruitment and mortality is often modeled by a positive, saturating term in P minus a proportional loss term (net turnover structure).
- Seasonality or periodic resources are indicated by sinusoidal dependence on t multiplying P (forcing acts on per-capita rates rather than adding absolute counts).
- Constant harvesting/stocking appears as an additive constant in dP_dt, which dominates dynamics near P ≈ 0 and can create extinction thresholds.
- Proportional harvesting/mortality appears as a linear term in P added to growth, shifting the effective intrinsic growth rate and equilibrium.
- Nonstationary environments can be represented by coefficients that drift with t (e.g., r(t) = c0 + c1*t), leading to moving equilibria and transient tracking.
- Crowding effects that intensify smoothly can be captured with exp(c*P) or log(c/P) factors, producing strong suppression without a hard cutoff.
